  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_58cb6f05-2b6d-43f9-a62d-95ba206b129f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText12987305723512128338" style="display:none">Light Yagami is an ace student with great prospects--and he's bored out of his mind. But all that changes when he finds the Death Note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami death god. Any human whose name is written in the notebook dies, and now Light has vowed to use the power of the Death Note to rid the world of evil. But when criminals begin dropping dead, the authorities send the legendary detective L to track down the killer. With L hot on his heels, will Light lose sight of his noble goal...or his life?</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">They don't really, some people think that the black ones are prettier and some people like the art on the 40 odd singles, it's the same story just in <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">They don't really, some people think that the black ones are prettier and some people like the art on the 40 odd singles, it's the same story just in different books. It's also just a little cheaper to buy the black editions also can be easier to just have 1 book for two volumes. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <span id="freeText7107099441175478987" style="display:none">4****<br /><br />A great, smart, and twisty graphic novel! <br /><br />Light Yagami is the top student with great ambition- and he is bored out of his mind. His monotonous life changes when he finds the Death note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami- a death God. Any human who touches the death note is able to the death god who owns it. Light is able to see a death god named Ryuk. The death note enables the death of the human whose name is written in the book. As Light discovers it’s power, he vows to rid the world of evil and become worshipped like a God. <br /><br />When people start to die, Light finds an enemy in a secretive investigator only known as L. This book allows the reader to see the power hunger, intelligence, and competition between the two men. We are witness to Light’s moral decline as he plans to win the game between him and L.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12108047230929950101"><b>3.5/5</b><br/><br/>I read the first two volumes of Death Note in one sitting and I really enjoyed the cat and mouse dynamic between Light and L. Ryuk was by far my favorite character - I loved his snide commentary. I kind of wish the art had been in color, although I know that's not common in manga.   <span id="freeText12108047230929950101" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5</b><br /><br />I read the first two volumes of Death Note in one sitting and I really enjoyed the cat and mouse dynamic between Light and L. Ryuk was by far my favorite character - I loved his snide commentary. I kind of wish the art had been in color, although I know that's not common in manga. I also realized that I don't enjoy manga as much as I did when I was younger. I found myself sometimes ignoring the pictures and just reading the text. Maybe I'm just too used to reading regular books, haha. Overall, this was a good time and I'm glad I read it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5445877067501498219">4.5 🌟<br/><br/>I can’t believe I’ve waited this long to pick this one up. It’s so dark and intense, violent and mysterious, I LOVED IT. </span>

<div id="review_1523894572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1523894572" />
    <a title="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35853271-sonja"><img alt="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484219542p2/35853271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523894572?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" href="/user/show/35853271-sonja">Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421539645" href="/book/show/9267091-death-note">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=awesomesauce">awesomesauce</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=love-this-so-much">love-this-so-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=pure-genius">pure-genius</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523894572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10523167115168554581"><b>4.5 out of 5 stars.</b><br/><b>
  <blockquote>The human whose name is written in this note shall die.</blockquote>
</b>I couldn't put <i>Death Note</i> down once I started it; I had to continue flipping the pages until it ended. <br/>I love the main character Light Yagami; he's a mix between Hermione, Lord Voldemort, the Joker and Batman, as weird as that all sounds. He's very clever and intelligent, however he does very morally-questionable things.<br/><br/>Good and bad are not as simply divided as black and white; there are grey areas too. And Light is a </span>
  <span id="freeText10523167115168554581" style="display:none"><b>4.5 out of 5 stars.</b><br /><b>
  <blockquote>The human whose name is written in this note shall die.</blockquote>
</b>I couldn't put <i>Death Note</i> down once I started it; I had to continue flipping the pages until it ended. <br />I love the main character Light Yagami; he's a mix between Hermione, Lord Voldemort, the Joker and Batman, as weird as that all sounds. He's very clever and intelligent, however he does very morally-questionable things.<br /><br />Good and bad are not as simply divided as black and white; there are grey areas too. And Light is a perfect example of that. <br /><br />The premise of <i>Death Note</i> was very promising and it was executed extremely well! In the beginning there is a bit of an information dump because the principles and the power of the Death Note need to be explained. However, after the basics were revealed, the pace quickly picked up and the manga became addictive!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"I'm creating a criminal-free utopia... over which I plan to reign like a god for long time."</b>
</blockquote>Light wants to use the Death Note to make the world a better place. In the beginning his intentions are good, but at a certain moment he becomes a bit power-hungry. The power to kill people, by simply writing their name down in the Death Note with their face in his mind, makes him arrogant. He can deliver punishments to those who are "bad" and reward those who are "good" by not killing them. <br /><br />The whole abstract idea of <i>good vs bad</i> and <i>right vs wrong</i> is challenged. As a reader it made me consider my own values and what I would have done if I was Light. It also made me think about the value of life and whether any human beings as individuals have the right to kill another human being. Even if the ones being killed are the "bad guys" is that enough of a justification to become a "bad guy" by killing them? <br /><br /><i>Death Note</i> gave me a lot of food for thought. It has a lot more depth than I thought it would have on first sight. <u>I definitely recommend it! The artwork is beautiful, and the story is magnificent!</u><br /><br />When I was reading <i>Death Note</i> I thought of what Gandalf said in <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i>. It seems very fitting.<blockquote>
  <b>"Many that live deserve death. And some that die deserve life. Can you give it to them? Then do not be too eager to deal out death in judgment. For even the very wise cannot see all ends."</b>
</blockquote><br />Whilst reading <i>Death Note</i> my mind also wandered to this beautiful poem by r.m. drake:<blockquote>
  <b>love what loves you<br />but never hate what<br />hates you, for hate<br />is the burden to<br />exhaust the stars<br />in you.<br /><br />r.m. drake</b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="10523167115168554581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/52343138-lauren">Lauren</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52343138-lauren?shelf=manga">manga</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2104771619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14606862542452665887">Oooooooh, this was good. And I mean REALLY good! <br/><br/>Death Note follows Light Yagami who is a straight A student who finds the Death Note (a notebook accidentally dropped by Ryuk - a Shinigami death god) outside of his school. From there, he discovers what exactly the Death Note is capable of, and, what he himself is capable of (trust me, the power most definitely goes to his head!)<br/><br/>In the beginning, I can kind of understand his motive behind what he does (trying to rid the world of evil) however, on</span>
  <span id="freeText14606862542452665887" style="display:none">Oooooooh, this was good. And I mean REALLY good! <br /><br />Death Note follows Light Yagami who is a straight A student who finds the Death Note (a notebook accidentally dropped by Ryuk - a Shinigami death god) outside of his school. From there, he discovers what exactly the Death Note is capable of, and, what he himself is capable of (trust me, the power most definitely goes to his head!)<br /><br />In the beginning, I can kind of understand his motive behind what he does (trying to rid the world of evil) however, on knowing that there are FBI agents and the Japanese Task Force out to catch "Kira" (the name given to Light by the media), he then starts bumping them off too (people who are innocent and only doing their job!!) <br /><br />Death Note is incredibly creepy but you quickly get sucked into Light's mindset which compels you to continue reading. The other main character in this book is "L" who has made it his sole mission to foil "Kira" and stop his killing spree. It's a fantastic race against time with two very smart individuals going head to head with each other. <br /><br />And yes, I know it's heavily male-dominated but the story is just too darn good and this is why it deserves a solid 5 stars!!!! <br /><br />Two words to describe this book - addictive and compelling! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14606862542452665887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14347902592906196860" style="display:none">(So I'm leaving my pre-review, because my reaction was way too funny to be erased)<br /><br /> NO. IT CANT END THERE.<br /><br />QUICKLY WHERE THE FUCK CAN I FIND THE NEXT VOLUMES IN ENGLISH HERE IN FREAKING MEXICO.<br /><br />FUCK. BOOK DEPOSITORY. I NEED BOOK DEPOSITORY RIGHT NOW.<br /><br />Rtc because I need to find the next volumes 🙃<br /><br />〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰〰<br /><br />So now that I've calmed down (part of that was because I might be able to get the next volumes in a week or so), I think I'll be able to write a decent (and by that I mean weird) review.<br /><br />This was the first manga I've read, I watch anime but I had never ever read manga. And I simply loved that Ryuk was that one bitch that's just there for the drama. I loved the fact he was amused by everyone's stupidity.<br /><br />And he fucking wanted to play Mario golf. And he loves apples. If that's not cute I don't know what cute is.<br /><br />Oh, and also, I hope one day my eyeliner is as fierce as Ryuk's. <br /><br />That's all I have to say, now I'll go and wait for the week to pass so I can get the next volume.<br />THE HYPE FOR THIS THING IS REAL.</span>

  <span id="freeText7874490178425302284" style="display:none">My brother practically forced me into reading Death Note. But if you <i>do</i> like it, then you have to give me the money I spent on that book. <br />that's how sure he was because let me tell my brother is a financially conservative guy.<br /><br />Only a few chapters in, and I give him his money back.<br /><br />Death Note is officially my first manga read; a format I approached initially with a great deal of trepidation, based mostly on false assumptions of the content of manga. Even though the story did a lot of 'telling' rather than 'showing' it was good, you can't deny it worked for the storyline. <br /><br />The characters were very interesting and vibrant, I liked how I couldn't quite decide who's the bad guy over there, I rooted for both the protagonist and the antagonist. <br />(Side note: L's face creeped the shit outta me, man. I don't know if you guys know "The Grudge" the movie, remember? no? but good God L looks exactly like you know the boy whose father had killed him and the cat? that creepy women's son, RIGHT? Oh that movie used to give me a good deal of nightmares back in the day)<br /><br />A few points taken because the plot in the last chapter was unfeasible. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mean yeah you can tell somebody went through your stuff, but how did you know there were cameras and bugs?! that's impossible. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <span id="freeText11599531155233413385" style="display:none">My first proper adventure into reading Manga as part of the #GettingGraphic readalong and I have to say although it starts off quite cheesy I did find myself enjoying the sinister undertones and the fun manoeuvring that the main characters had to do by the end. <br /><br />We follow a young boy called Light who finds a DeathNote notebook. When he writes in a person's name whilst picturing them he can write out their death and cause it to happen. This turn of events allows Light to do a cleanse of the world's criminals, but it also alerts the authorities to someone killing these criminals, so Light has to hide his tracks...<br /><br />Overall it's a fairly standard art style and it's a fun story but it didn't quite wow me. I would like to keep reading to find out more, but I;m not yet fully hooked in. 3.5*s overall.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67783454-annie?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2895857811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8717260964352240523">⠀⠀✧ • ° . ◦ *⠀┊<b> three and three quarter stars. </b><br/><br/><br/><br/>⠀i thoroughly enjoyed this... so much that i ran to the library and got the remainder of the series. while this was extremely entertaining... i can’t help but to give it this star rating. it was great but could have been better, i guess. <br/><br/><br/><br/><i>
  <b><br/>⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀” look around you, and all you<br/>⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀ will see are people the world <br/>⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀ would be better off without. “</b>
</i><br/><br/><br/><br/>⠀<b>things i really enjoyed:</b><br/><br/><br/>❥ ┊<u>the premise.</u><br/>⠀⠀⠀⠀the idea of the the death note has always fascinated me. </span>
  <span id="freeText8717260964352240523" style="display:none">⠀⠀✧ • ° . ◦ *⠀┊<b> three and three quarter stars. </b><br /><br /><br /><br />⠀i thoroughly enjoyed this... so much that i ran to the library and got the remainder of the series. while this was extremely entertaining... i can’t help but to give it this star rating. it was great but could have been better, i guess. <br /><br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀” look around you, and all you<br />⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀ will see are people the world <br />⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀ would be better off without. “</b>
</i><br /><br /><br /><br />⠀<b>things i really enjoyed:</b><br /><br /><br />❥ ┊<u>the premise.</u><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀the idea of the the death note has always fascinated me. as someone who has almost no interest in anime or manga i couldn’t help but be beyond intrigued. the ability to write a name &amp; act of death in a notebook is nothing less than clever. even though several years have passed, this is still such an original concept. <br /><br />❥ ┊<u>the cast.</u><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀for what is worth, the cast was pretty enjoyable. i really enjoyed our main character, light. he’s the type of character i love to read about. ryuk is adorable and kind of reminds me of venom. L is the cutest bean i’ve ever seen and i would die for him. i didn’t have any complaints about the side characters as they were all fairly realistic. <br /><br />❥ ┊<u>the plot.</u><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀the plot was pretty solid. i had absolutely no idea what this was about so it couldn’t deviate from expectations &amp; disappoint. i feel like the second volume was a little more bland than the first but it was still extremely interesting.<br /><br />❥ ┊<u>the thought.</u><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀the thought put into this is incredible. many of the actions and choices presented in this are air tight. they’re thought out——fool proof. i know this is kind of applauding a fish for swimming but this story can get pretty complex and i appreciate the author taking the time to think everything through. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />⠀<b>things i <i>didn’t</i> enjoy:</b><br /><br /><br />❥ ┊<u>missing piece.</u><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀this is where things get weird. i don’t have anything to complain about yet i feel as if this could be better. i don’t know why or how but this seems like it’s missing something. maybe i’ll come up with something as i progress in the series but. who knows. <br /><br />❥ ┊<u>second volume’s plot.</u><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀don’t get me wrong, i enjoyed this plot but i wish it was a bit more like the first. i think i just wished the death note was used more or was more of the focus than the investigation.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀<b>overall,</b> this was pretty great and a good choice for my first manga. to clarify the ratings, the first volume was about four stars and the second was about three and a half stars. there’s no doubt i’m continuing the series &amp; would recommend this to anyone. </span>

<div id="review_1378943376" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1378943376" />
    <a title="gio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23204207-gio"><img alt="gio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597613414p2/23204207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1378943376?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gio" href="/user/show/23204207-gio">gio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23204207-gio?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1378943376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6719892059775317130">Manga experiment?<br/>Kind of. When I was a child I'd spend hours watching anime. Considering that I love reading and I love art one would hink I'm used to manga. I'm not, and for a simple reason: I'd rather spend my money on a book, that I know it'll take me at least a couple of hours to read, rather than on something that is quite expensive and I can read in one hour. <br/><br/>I decided to read Death note because I was curious. I was definitely curious and I'm not enjoying reading much these days because of</span>
  <span id="freeText6719892059775317130" style="display:none">Manga experiment?<br />Kind of. When I was a child I'd spend hours watching anime. Considering that I love reading and I love art one would hink I'm used to manga. I'm not, and for a simple reason: I'd rather spend my money on a book, that I know it'll take me at least a couple of hours to read, rather than on something that is quite expensive and I can read in one hour. <br /><br />I decided to read Death note because I was curious. I was definitely curious and I'm not enjoying reading much these days because of exams and stuff, sadly. And in a way, I liked it.<br /><br />Disclaimer: if the lack of female characters enrage you don't try this one. In fact I knocked down the rating a bit because it's rather sexist. <br /><br />Also, I still don't enjoy much this format, because I need a story that flows as a whole, and this kind of narration doesn't give me much of that. <br /><br />Those issues aside this was pretty good. The art is fabulous and really detailed. This might sound strange but I've always envied how hair is drawn in anime/manga, because it's so detailed and has a marvelous effect that I wish I could obtain in my drawings. My weirdness aside, I really really liked the art at least.<br /><br />I loved the plot because it reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>, by Schwab. And this mainly because there's no good or bad, but it's all morally gray (and I love morally gray stuff, I revel in it) and because the Light/L game reminds me of Eli and Victor. I mean, this kind of battle they have, a bit like a game of chess in which real people are the pawns, is pretty exciting. And twisted. Can you see the heart eyes?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6719892059775317130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17855294262127915429">(Hmm.....I did write a review but it didn't post)<br/><br/>Anyways........this was my first manga! This particular notebook was dropped by a Shinigami, a death god. Apparently whoever is in ownership of this book has the power to kill people.   <span id="freeText17855294262127915429" style="display:none">(Hmm.....I did write a review but it didn't post)<br /><br />Anyways........this was my first manga! It did take a minute for me to get used to reading the other way lol, but once I got the hang of it I really enjoyed it! <br /><br />Light Yagami is a high school student in Japan who comes across a notebook. This particular notebook was dropped by a Shinigami, a death god. Apparently whoever is in ownership of this book has the power to kill people. Once Light understands what he's capable of doing, he decides to play God and rid the world of all the abhorrent people who "deserve it". In his mind he feels he's doing a great thing and with that, the people will then be so scared to do anything bad for fear of getting killed, resulting in a sort of utopia. Light believes he will be revered so it shocks him when he realizes the police are after HIM. (because after all, he is still killing people) <br /><br />If there's anything to critique about this story it's that everything is laid out and explained (almost step by step) giving the reader nothing to really figure out on their own. What I did end up liking, surprisingly, was Shinigami. He may have been a death god but I really liked his amusing sarcasm. And aesthetically speaking, I love these Black Editions......I may have to add them to my collection. :)</span>

<div id="review_198398511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198398511" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/361125-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506683246p2/361125.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198398511?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/361125-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421539645" href="/book/show/9267091-death-note">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/361125-greg?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/361125-greg?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/361125-greg?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198398511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6069709846693387369">At nearly 400 pages, this is quite a tome for a comic book, but the length adds value for money to what is, overall, a very intelligent and thought-provoking narrative. Essentially, it deals with the ethical and philosophical issues that arise when, suddenly given the power of life or death over other people, what would one do with it? It’s also a tale of two brilliant young minds trying to outwit each other, their tactics and forward-planning making the story more complex and absorbing as it un</span>
  <span id="freeText6069709846693387369" style="display:none">At nearly 400 pages, this is quite a tome for a comic book, but the length adds value for money to what is, overall, a very intelligent and thought-provoking narrative. Essentially, it deals with the ethical and philosophical issues that arise when, suddenly given the power of life or death over other people, what would one do with it? It’s also a tale of two brilliant young minds trying to outwit each other, their tactics and forward-planning making the story more complex and absorbing as it unfolds – a pleasure for this fan of tactical computer games and an ex-role-playing gamer. <br /><br />The artwork is more natural than a lot of other manga, which tends to juvenalise adult characters by giving them large eyes and otherwise childish faces (I’m thinking of Kentaro Yabuki’s <i>Black Cat</i> series, for example). In <i>Death note</i>, adults look like adults, while the lead character, Light Yagami, is a teenager who looks his age (he’s 17). Only the enigmatic character, L, is more difficult to age. He looks no older than Light Yagami yet his knowledge and reasoning is that of an adult. His behaviour, at times, does seem juvenile, such as when he squats on an armchair in bare feet while discussing the case of Kira with members of Japan’s National Police Agency (pp. 264-75) and, at one point, L actually describes himself as ‘childish’ (p. 265), but my guess is that he’s either a child prodigy in his late teens or that he’s in his early 20s but looks younger. <br /><br />The change from using colour to depict the realm of the shinigami to using black-and-white for the human world when Ryuk enters it (following p. 8) accentuates the dark path that Light Yagami embarks upon soon after finding the Death Note. To somebody more used to reading full-colour comics, this difference must seem more dramatic, but for people (like me) who grew up reading the largely monochrome British comics of the 1970s and 1980s, this is a familiar visual experience. <br /><br />My only real complaint about the story is that Light Yagami recovers too quickly from his scary initial encounter with Ryuk on pp. 16-18 and even seems to view it positively. Perhaps some teens really wouldn’t be all that scared if they suddenly met the shinigami since he resembles a kind of weird cross between a goth and Bill Kaulitz of Tokio Hotel, with his skinny form, black skin-tight clothing, large silver belt-buckle and wild mop of black hair. However, Ryuk also resembles something straight out of an H. P. Lovecraft story with his fish eyes and many sharp, pointed teeth, while he also sports wings and a ring of metal piercings that attach his clothes to his body around his neck. I can’t see myself recovering from a sight like that quite so quickly or accepting that it really is a god of death – surely, I would’ve thought that I was losing my marbles rather than think the apparition was real! However, once you get over the hurdle of this rather unlikely meeting, the rest of the book unfolds well and is a fun read.<br /><br />I’m looking forward to reading the next volume in the series!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6069709846693387369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4931022881444723547" style="display:none">All these years and I never picked up Death Note. What is wrong with me?!<br /><br />Well, I’m glad I finally did (we’ll thank the boyfriend for having the beautiful Black Edition!). This is everything but what I imagined. My knowledge of Death Note before picking up the book went as far as that: there’s a notebook where you can write the name of someone you want dead. The end. <br /><br /><i>Laugh uncontrollably.</i><br /><br />I WAS SO WRONG.<br /><br />I mean, I did get the notebook bit but Death Note is about so much more! It is about what is right and what is wrong, about love and power, about being in the light (see what I did here?) and the shadow. This has kept me so eager to read that I would try to imagine impossible scenarios all the time. I don’t read mangas but I am glad I made an exception for this one. Sooooo good! <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2508159309045221794">First of all Jon don't hate me for reading this before I got it for Christmas. (read it online). Nevertheless these black editions are beautiful and will look great on my bookshelf. <br/><br/>Now for the review: This is an amazing, very unique story. In fact, it was just what I was looking for at the time. Part mythical and fantasy equal part mystery. A young adult finds a notebook called the death note and is able to kill people by simply writing their name with their face in mind. He can also choose how</span>
  <span id="freeText2508159309045221794" style="display:none">First of all Jon don't hate me for reading this before I got it for Christmas. (read it online). Nevertheless these black editions are beautiful and will look great on my bookshelf. <br /><br />Now for the review: This is an amazing, very unique story. In fact, it was just what I was looking for at the time. Part mythical and fantasy equal part mystery. A young adult finds a notebook called the death note and is able to kill people by simply writing their name with their face in mind. He can also choose how and when this death occurs. His new mission in life becomes to rid the world of all evil and have a perfect utopia. That is until another young detective named L is on the case and they are consistently trying to throw each other off. It's a battle of good versus evil but you have no idea what side to be one. I also am simultaneously watching the anime as I read. All and all this is a great story and I will later have a full series review on the 6th volume when I make it there. <br /><br />Read it though, it's a great story. I do however recommend buying it to support the author and the translators, I only read it online because I know I got the first vol. for Christmas. If you do decide to read this let me know your thoughts!</span>

<div id="review_2502094815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2502094815" />
    <a title="Phee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26480778-phee"><img alt="Phee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580467651p2/26480778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2502094815?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phee" href="/user/show/26480778-phee">Phee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26480778-phee?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2502094815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15561178815450804091">Obviously being the huge Deathnote fan that I am, nothing but a 5 star rating for this. For me Deathnote is one of the most addictive, powerful, and engrossing stories I’ve had the pleasure of experiencing. The characters are fantastic and the whole cat and mouse arc of Light vs L is one of favourites of all time. L is my kindred spirit and my cake loving self loves him dearly. <br/>If anyone has been debating giving this a go, then I urge you too. You won’t regret it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2502094815">
  <td colspan="2">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047395-lyndsay?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2910765938" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1450462099863640820">Cole is always bugging me to read more manga and he really wants to watch the Death Note anime with me. But I wanted to read the manga first so I'm so happy that I was finally able to get around to it in July. I loved loved loved this. I was sucked in from the very first page and the only reason I didn't finish it all in one sitting is because I literally fell asleep staying up late trying to finish it.<br/><br/>If you don't know, this series follows a boy named Light who finds a notebook one day and lear</span>
  <span id="freeText1450462099863640820" style="display:none">Cole is always bugging me to read more manga and he really wants to watch the Death Note anime with me. But I wanted to read the manga first so I'm so happy that I was finally able to get around to it in July. I loved loved loved this. I was sucked in from the very first page and the only reason I didn't finish it all in one sitting is because I literally fell asleep staying up late trying to finish it.<br /><br />If you don't know, this series follows a boy named Light who finds a notebook one day and learns that it is a Death Note. He finds out that if he writes a person's name in it and how they're going to die, then they will die. He decides to use this Death Note to rid the world of evil people. But things get a little dicey when the police start noticing the deaths of all these criminals and feel that someone is out there killing them.<br /><br />I just have to say that this is one of the most action-packed books I've ever read. From one page to the next, I had no idea what was going to happen. This bind-up contains volumes 1 and 2 of 12 and so much happened in just this volume that I have no idea what the scope of this story is actually going to be. I just got so invested in these characters and this story that I didn't want to put it down and upon finishing it, I immediately ordered volumes 2 and 3. I can't wait to continue on with this series and then eventually watch the anime because this was fantastic.<br /><br />If you're a big manga reader, you've probably already read this. But if you haven't, I'd highly recommend doing so. If you aren't a big manga reader, I'd say this would be an excellent place to start because it will suck you in from page one and you won't want to stop.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1450462099863640820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167255488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167255488" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/933518-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269638796p2/933518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167255488?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/933518-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782505009054" href="/book/show/10321647-death-note">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167255488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10407852165549060721">My FIRST MANGA!!<br/>Historically, I've enthusiastically avoided Manga because of the assumptions I've always adhered to regarding the genre's deeply questionable proclivity to highlight particular regions of the young female anatomy (You know EXACTLY what I'm talking about if you've ever paged through one). <br/>Not wanting to associate myself with such inappropriately prurient material, I therefore decided long ago to give the multitude of Manga publications, which CONSTANTLY devour more and more shelf </span>
  <span id="freeText10407852165549060721" style="display:none">My FIRST MANGA!!<br />Historically, I've enthusiastically avoided Manga because of the assumptions I've always adhered to regarding the genre's deeply questionable proclivity to highlight particular regions of the young female anatomy (You know EXACTLY what I'm talking about if you've ever paged through one). <br />Not wanting to associate myself with such inappropriately prurient material, I therefore decided long ago to give the multitude of Manga publications, which CONSTANTLY devour more and more shelf space in comic and book stores, a WIDE margin in my daily wanderings among the store shelves. <br /><br />Well, someone on the Comic Geek Speak podcast (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.comicgeekspeak.com">www.comicgeekspeak.com</a>) raved about how good this book is, and SWORE it wasn't unseemly in any way, so, based on this recommendation, I picked it up. <br />And I must say it is really really good!!<br />I find I like the art very much, and the story is very intriguing. The conflict between Light and "L" reminds of the episode of Star Trek wherein Kirk and a Romulan Captain square off in an epic battle of wits and combat strategy. <br />The glimpses into Japanese mythology are also very interesting. <br />All in all I'd say this is an awesome introduction into the world of Manga that won't make you feel like you need good hot shower after you're done reading it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10407852165549060721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1503414892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1503414892" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10697179-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549097p2/10697179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1503414892?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/10697179-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1503414892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11901774553587569516">CAN. WE. JUST.<br/>This was A.M.A.Z.I.N.G.<br/>Honestly wow. My first experience reading Manga and I honestly put it off because I worried the right to left back of the book to the beginning would be too weird but it was so easy. <br/>I am sad I got this from the library because I want to own it but I bought the second Volume and I can't wait. <br/><br/><i>Around The Year in 52 Books Challenge #50 - A book originally written in a language other than English</i></span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Fem7htBkzkVWVkrToT0XI/QKhDC3m8x0uPHAUjZXV7I1tJX9OyeCSfEaT0Juy8ePlz7Z8RsbpgGkQZuI35RtyQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j8l2kki8hMovCr47L565FVy6bnByNQDnb4DS/LKYWZivlFjpo//IxohGu6rgaGm5P44zsd61apJzMIkmW1tj4w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11542640559752027205">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText11542640559752027205" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>
